### Round 1 | planner | planner_initial

- diagnosis: Task: infer the most likely AIE mechanism (ICT, TICT, ESIPT, neutral aromatic, or unknown) for the given molecule. Based on the provided prepared structure (ready; 66 atoms, 5 aromatic rings, 8 rotatable bonds, neutral singlet) and its tetraphenyl/triarylethylene-like scaffold with methoxy substituents plus an aldehyde acceptor, the working top1 hypothesis is TICT/RIM-driven AIE: in solution, multiple aryl rotations can open nonradiative channels and/or allow a twisted CT-like S1; in aggregates these motions are restricted, enhancing emission. The runner-up is neutral aromatic/RIM without pronounced CT, because the system is largely hydrocarbon-like and the donor–acceptor contrast may be modest; also high planarity proxy could indicate LE-dominated emission with aggregation restricting motion rather than forming a strong CT state. Top1 remains uncertain because we do not yet know (i) whether S1 has significant charge-transfer character (dipole change, NTO separation), (ii) whether S1 favors twisting vs planarization relative to S0, and (iii) whether the aldehyde meaningfully participates in the excitation. Evidence to separate TICT vs neutral aromatic: a single baseline S0-optimized geometry with S1 vertical excitation (oscillator strength, excitation energy) plus qualitative CT diagnostics (orbital/NTO localization, dipole change) from the microscopic run, together with a macro-level structural/mechanistic assessment of likely RIM vs CT pathways. Macro can qualitatively map structure-to-mechanism expectations and flag competing AIE pathways; Microscopic can provide one bounded baseline S0/S1 computation on the shared prepared conformer but cannot (in this first round) explore conformer/torsion sensitivity or aggregation/packing explicitly. First round should gather both: macro for rapid mechanistic priors and microscopic for first-principles hints about S1 character that discriminate TICT vs neutral-aromatic AIE.

- diagnosis: Top1 is now TICT (0.48) vs top2 neutral aromatic (0.28), with ICT (0.21) close behind. Latest evidence partially weakens the earlier TICT lead: macro proxies show high S0 planarity for the selected conformer (planarity_proxy ~0.95) and only moderate donor–acceptor strength (hetero_atom_count=3; donor_acceptor_partition_proxy~0.5). Microscopic baseline shows a strongly allowed lowest vertical excitation (S1 f~0.44 at 3.20 eV; lowest_state_is_bright), which is more immediately compatible with an LE/neutral-aromatic picture than with a classic dark CT state at the bottom, though this is not decisive without CT descriptors and torsional sensitivity. The neutral-aromatic challenger is strengthened by the combination of high planarity proxy and bright lowest excitation. ICT remains plausible but is not confirmed; the sizeable S0 dipole (~6.6 D) is suggestive yet not diagnostic of excited-state ICT. Key remaining discriminator between TICT vs neutral aromatic (and vs ICT) is whether the lowest emissive/relaxed excited state becomes CT-like upon twisting and whether excitation/CT metrics change strongly with torsion (i.e., torsion-driven state switching). Verifier supplementation is still missing. Closure justification is missing. Given round budget is ample (20 remaining), the best next action is a single bounded microscopic parse step to extract CT descriptors from the already-computed baseline bundle, which is the cheapest discriminative evidence to separate TICT/ICT vs neutral aromatic.

Reasoning summary: From the shared structure context, the molecule is a multi-aryl, highly substituted conjugated system with several formally rotatable inter-aryl single bonds (rotatable_bond_count=8; torsion_candidate_count=8) and multiple aromatic rings (aromatic_ring_count=5). This topology supports the presence of low-frequency torsions that could enable twisting between donor-like anisole rings and an acceptor-like benzaldehyde fragment, a prerequisite for TICT-type geometries. However, the provided geometry proxies show a relatively high planarity_proxy (~0.95) and compactness_proxy (~0.93) for the selected conformer, which is more consistent with a comparatively planar/extended conjugated arrangement in S0 for that conformer (i.e., not strongly twisted at baseline). The donor/acceptor partition proxy (~0.5) and low hetero atom count (3: two methoxy O plus one aldehyde O) indicate only moderate intrinsic D–A strength; thus TICT is plausible via rotors, but not strongly compelled by an obvious strong push–pull motif at the macro/topology level alone.

- diagnosis: Round 2 update (budget: 2/20 used; 19 rounds remaining). Top1 is now neutral aromatic (0.37) vs top2 TICT (0.34); ICT remains a close third (0.25). Latest evidence: the attempted microscopic CT-descriptor extraction from the existing baseline bundle failed to retrieve the key CT observables (electron–hole separation, CT amount indices, state character labels), so it provides no new direct CT/LE discriminator. Indirectly, this shifts weight toward neutral aromatic because (i) the molecule’s selected conformer is quite planar (planarity_proxy~0.95) and (ii) the lowest vertical S1 is strongly allowed (f~0.44, lowest state is bright), both more typical of LE-dominated aromatics than canonical dark TICT minima—while not ruling out TICT given many rotors. Effect on top2 challenger (TICT): weakened relative to neutral aromatic because no CT character evidence emerged and the baseline photophysics look LE-like; still plausible structurally due to high torsional freedom. Additional candidate affected (ICT): held moderately high because the D–A motif and S0 dipole remain compatible with some ICT, but cannot be confirmed without excited-state CT metrics. Key remaining discriminator for neutral aromatic vs TICT: whether low-lying excited states show charge-transfer character and/or become more CT-like upon twisting (torsion dependence / CT indices) versus remaining primarily LE across torsions. Verifier supplementation: still missing. Closure justification: still collecting/insufficient because the intended discriminative CT descriptors were not obtained. Best next action: call Verifier to obtain external discriminator criteria/precedent for this specific scaffold class (triarylethylene-like / polyaryl with aldehyde + anisole donors) and to identify what experimental signatures (solvatochromism, dual emission, viscosity dependence, solid-state vs solution behavior) most strongly separate LE/RIM from (T)ICT in similar molecules; this is now higher value given local extraction could not provide CT indices from current artifacts.

- diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (0.52) vs top2=ICT (0.23); TICT is now third (0.18). The verifier supplement is close-family and provides genuinely new discriminative context: (i) AIE in propeller-shaped polyaryl/TPE-like luminogens is commonly RIM/RIR with LE emission and minimal solvatochromism (supports neutral aromatic), and (ii) classical TICT requires strong donors and typically shows strong solvatochromism/dual emission/low-f CT emission; OMe donors are noted as generally too weak for classical TICT (challenges TICT). A separate close-family card indicates OMe/aldehyde substituted TPE analogs tend to remain LE-dominated with at most modest ICT while retaining RIM, which pushes probability mass from TICT toward neutral aromatic and (secondarily) ICT. Evidence is not an exact-compound hit (documented limitation), so it is strong for the pairwise mechanism prior but still analog-based. Closure justification is not yet sufficient for a decisive close because it lacks direct molecule-specific excited-state CT/torsion dependence observables; however, verifier supplementation for the current pair is sufficient and suggests a better targeted internal follow-up (torsion snapshots to test whether twisting produces CT-like dark states). Not ready to finalize.

### Round 4 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 4/20 (17 remaining). Top1=neutral aromatic (0.46) vs Top2=ICT (0.27); TICT is third (0.19). Latest evidence (microscopic torsion snapshots on dihedral dih_4_5_6_7 at 0/45/90°) shows the lowest excited state is dark (f=0.0) across all snapshots, with the first bright state appearing higher (first bright at ~3.8946 eV with f~0.0767). This does not match a classic TICT discriminator of torsion-induced emergence of a new low-lying CT/TICT state that becomes dominant upon twisting; instead, it suggests a stable low-lying dark state that is not strongly modulated by torsion within this scan. This strengthens the neutral-aromatic/LE-RIM picture (and weakens TICT as a torsion-triggered switching mechanism) while leaving room for modest ICT (aldehyde/OMe push–pull) that could still be present but is not evidenced as a torsion-driven state inversion. Key remaining discriminator between neutral aromatic and ICT: molecule-specific CT character metrics (electron–hole separation / Δdipole) or experimental solvatochromism/viscosity dependence; current torsion scan provides state-ordering/brightness but not CT indices. Verifier supplementation is sufficient (close-family precedent) and remains mixed-but-high-IG; closure justification is still collecting because the internal torsion observable is only partially discriminative for neutral aromatic vs ICT.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.46

### Round 5 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 5/20 (16 remaining). Top1=neutral aromatic (0.52) vs top2=ICT (0.26); TICT is a weaker third (0.13). Latest evidence (parsed torsion snapshots at 0/45/90°) strengthens the neutral-aromatic/LE-RIM picture because S1 is consistently dark (f=0.0) and twisting pushes the first bright state to higher index (from S2 at 0/45° to S4 at 90°), consistent with torsion-induced loss of oscillator strength/decoupling rather than a torsion-induced CT/TICT state takeover. This weakens the ICT challenger slightly (no clear CT-brightening or CT-state takeover signature) while still leaving room for modest ICT mixing (acceptor aldehyde + donors) given missing CT metrics. Key remaining discriminator (neutral aromatic vs ICT) is direct CT character of the emissive bright state(s): electron–hole separation/Δμ or solvent-polarity sensitivity proxies. Verifier supplementation is sufficient (close-family precedent), while closure justification remains collecting for the neutral aromatic vs ICT pair. Best next action is an additional low-cost internal microscopic observable that can serve as a CT proxy within available registry actions: run a small conformer bundle to see whether any low-energy conformer exhibits a substantially different bright-state pattern (consistent with more polarized/ICT conformers).

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.52

- task_instruction: Microscopic: run exactly one registry-backed action `run_conformer_bundle` on the shared prepared structure (f06edabe57ee). Keep it small/bounded (e.g., max_conformers=5). For each conformer, compute vertical states 1–5 and report: (a) whether S1 is dark vs bright, (b) first_bright_state_index and its energy/f, and (c) any conformer-to-conformer shifts suggesting increased polarization/ICT (e.g., consistently lower-energy bright state with altered ordering). Goal: discriminate neutral aromatic (robust LE manifold across conformers) vs ICT (subset of conformers with more CT-like/shifted bright state behavior). No excited-state optimization; no heavy DFT.

### Round 6 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Round 6/20 (15 rounds remaining). Top1=neutral aromatic (0.61) vs Top2=ICT (0.23). Latest evidence (microscopic run_conformer_bundle; 5 low-energy conformers) strengthens the current top1: across conformers, S1 remains the lowest bright state with high oscillator strength (f≈0.44–0.47) and minimal dispersion in S1 energy (spread 0.032 eV) and brightness (sensitivity 0.033). This robustness is more consistent with an LE-dominated neutral-aromatic manifold (RIM/AIE) than with ICT, which would more likely show stronger conformer-selective polarization/state reordering. The runner-up (ICT) is correspondingly weakened (not eliminated) because direct CT metrics are still unavailable. Additional candidate impacted: TICT is further downweighted because the conformer data do not show darkening or state switching characteristic of torsion/conformer-activated TICT, aligning with close-family literature that OMe/aldehyde systems are rarely classical TICT. Key remaining discriminator for neutral aromatic vs ICT is still direct CT/polarization evidence (electron–hole separation, Δμ, or experimental solvatochromism/viscosity dependence). Verifier supplementation is sufficient (close-family) but not targeted to neutral aromatic vs ICT; closure justification remains collecting for the current pair, since we still lack direct CT descriptors. Given the internal tool limits on CT indices, the best next action is a Verifier pass explicitly targeted to neutral aromatic vs ICT discriminators in OMe/aldehyde-substituted TPE/triarylethylene analogs (expected solvatochromism magnitude, Lippert–Mataga slopes, Stokes shifts) to decide whether to treat ICT as minor mixing or a primary mechanism label.

This supports (not challenges) the current top1 and shrinks the ICT hypothesis to a secondary-modulator role. - diagnosis: Top1=neutral aromatic (0.72) vs top2=ICT (0.18). The verifier supplement for neutral aromatic vs ICT is close-family but materially discriminative: it provides quantitative solvent-response/Lippert–Mataga benchmarks for OMe/aldehyde TPE-like systems, indicating LE/RIM-dominant emission with only weak ICT mixing (Δμ ~3–6 D; solvatochromism usually <20–30 nm), while strong ICT assignments require much larger shifts and Δμ. This supports (not challenges) the current top1 and shrinks the ICT hypothesis to a secondary-modulator role. Closure justification is now sufficient for the current pair (neutral aromatic vs ICT) in the sense of mechanism-label choice, though exact-compound CT metrics remain missing.
